<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WebberCanada2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2863" data-file-width="1909" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WebberCanada2011.jpg/220px-WebberCanada2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WebberCanada2011.jpg/330px-WebberCanada2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/WebberCanada2011.jpg/440px-WebberCanada2011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<a href="/wiki/Mark_Webber" title="Mark Webber">Mark Webber</a>, Vettel's teammate, finished third in the championship for the second season in succession.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <b>2011 Formula One season</b> was the 62nd season of <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">FIA Formula One</a> motor racing. The original calendar for the 2011 Formula One World Championship consisted of twenty rounds,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> including the inaugural running of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Grand_Prix" title="Indian Grand Prix">Indian Grand Prix</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_2011_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-India_2011-2">[2]</a></sup> before the cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Bahrain Grand Prix">Bahrain Grand Prix</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pirelli" title="Pirelli">Pirelli</a> returned to the sport as <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_tyres" title="Formula One tyres">tyre supplier</a> for all teams, taking over from <a href="/wiki/Bridgestone" title="Bridgestone">Bridgestone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMSC230610_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMSC230610-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a> was the reigning Constructors' Champion. Red Bull Racing's <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Vettel" title="Sebastian Vettel">Sebastian Vettel</a> was the defending Drivers' Champion, one of five World Champions appearing on the grid. Vettel won his second World Championship at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Japanese_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Japanese Grand Prix">2011 Japanese Grand Prix</a>, becoming the youngest driver, at 24 years and 98 days, to do so. Red Bull Racing won the Constructors' Championship.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teams_and_drivers">Teams and drivers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Formula_One_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Teams and drivers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After a <a href="/wiki/FIA%E2%80%93FOTA_dispute" title="FIA–FOTA dispute">dispute</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One_Teams_Association" title="Formula One Teams Association">Formula One Teams Association</a> (FOTA) and the FIA in the first half of <a href="/wiki/2009_Formula_One_season" title="2009 Formula One season">2009</a>, a new <a href="/wiki/Concorde_Agreement" title="Concorde Agreement">Concorde Agreement</a> was signed on 1 August 2009 by the then FIA president <a href="/wiki/Max_Mosley" title="Max Mosley">Max Mosley</a> and all of the existing teams at the time. The new agreement provides for a continuation of the terms of the 1998 agreement, and runs until 31 December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The FIA published a provisional entry list on 30 November 2010, which was revised on 2 December 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FIA021210_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FIA021210-5">[5]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_entries_process">New entries process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Formula_One_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: New entries process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following <a href="/wiki/US_F1_Team" title="US F1 Team">USF1</a>'s inability to make the grid in <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_season" title="2010 Formula One season">2010</a>, the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Internationale_de_l%27Automobile" title="Fédération Internationale de l'Automobile">FIA</a> opened a new selection process to find an additional team to occupy the empty slot, as well as possible reserve entrants for the event of other withdrawals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Full_grid_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Full_grid-50">[50]</a></sup> Fifteen entry bids were reported to have been received,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15_in_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-15_in-51">[51]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/ART_Grand_Prix" title="ART Grand Prix">ART Grand Prix</a>, winners of several championships in feeder series;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> previous 2010 applicants <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Grand_Prix" title="Stefan Grand Prix">Stefan Grand Prix</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Series_by_Renault" title="World Series by Renault">World Series by Renault</a> team <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epsilon_Euskadi" title="Epsilon Euskadi">Epsilon Euskadi</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> and a joint effort by <a href="/wiki/1997_Formula_One_season" title="1997 Formula One season">1997 World Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Villeneuve" title="Jacques Villeneuve">Jacques Villeneuve</a> with <a href="/wiki/Durango_(racing_team)" title="Durango (racing team)">Durango</a>, the former Italian <a href="/wiki/GP2_Series" title="GP2 Series">GP2</a> team that had encountered financial difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Villeneuve_Durango_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Villeneuve_Durango-55">[55]</a></sup> However, the number of applicants declined, as ART Grand Prix and <a href="/wiki/US_F1_Team#Rebirth_as_Cypher_Group" title="US F1 Team">Cypher</a>, the renamed USF1 operation, withdrew their entries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> and the FIA decided ahead of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2010 Italian Grand Prix">2010 Italian Grand Prix</a> that none of the prospective entrants met the minimum funding or engineering requirements, leaving the grid slot vacant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the confirmation that there would be no new additions to the grid for 2011, Joan Villadelprat of Epsilon Euskadi and <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Villeneuve" title="Jacques Villeneuve">Jacques Villeneuve</a> of the combined Villeneuve-Durango teams both announced that they would still attempt to join the grid for 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> exploring the possibilities of taking over an existing team. Villeneuve later admitted to considering possibilities outside of Formula One, including extending his <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationwide_Series" title="Nationwide Series">Nationwide Series</a> campaign, or moving to Australia to pursue opportunities in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/V8_Supercars" title="V8 Supercars">V8 Supercars</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Team_changes">Team changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Formula_One_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Team changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1109" data-file-width="1280" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg/220px-Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg/330px-Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg/440px-Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Renault_and_Lotus_2011_Malaysia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The season started with controversy when two teams using the Lotus name were entered onto the grid, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lotus_Renault_GP" title="Lotus Renault GP">Lotus Renault GP</a> (foreground) and <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus_(2010%E2%80%9311)" title="Team Lotus (2010–11)">Team Lotus</a> (background).</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>At the <a href="/wiki/2011_British_Grand_Prix" title="2011 British Grand Prix">British Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Ferrari" title="Scuderia Ferrari">Scuderia Ferrari</a> announced they would remove <a href="/wiki/Marlboro_(cigarette)" title="Marlboro (cigarette)">Marlboro</a> from their official team name in response to what they described as "recent concerns" regarding their association with the tobacco brand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marlboro_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marlboro-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
<li>In the week before the <a href="/wiki/2011_Korean_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Korean Grand Prix">Korean Grand Prix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Force_India" title="Force India">Force India</a> announced that the <a href="/wiki/Lucknow" title="Lucknow">Lucknow</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Sahara_India_Pariwar" title="Sahara India Pariwar">Sahara India Pariwar</a> conglomerate had purchased a 42.5% stake in the team, giving them co-ownership with team principal <a href="/wiki/Vijay_Mallya" title="Vijay Mallya">Vijay Mallya</a>. The team was subsequently renamed <a href="/wiki/Force_India" title="Force India">Sahara Force India</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sahara_Force_India_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sahara_Force_India-62">[62]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania</a> announced several major partnerships in November 2010. Chief among these was an arrangement that will see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Williams_F1" title="Williams F1">Williams</a> supply the <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">Murcia</a>-based team with transmission systems for the 2011 season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> whilst forming a partnership with Spanish businessman <a href="/wiki/Juan_Villalonga" title="Juan Villalonga">Juan Villalonga</a>, who was previously affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Minardi" title="Minardi">Minardi</a> as CEO of <a href="/wiki/Telef%C3%B3nica" title="Telefónica">Telefónica</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> In July 2011, Thesan Capital, a <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>-based investment company purchased a controlling stake in the team from owner <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ram%C3%B3n_Carabante" title="José Ramón Carabante">José Ramón Carabante</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Thesan Capital announced the team's operations would continue as they had before the purchase, and that they had no plans to change the team name or alter its operational structure. In a statement released to the media, Thesan Capital described their intentions as making the team "more Spanish" and settling the team within Spain;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> the team had previously been supported by a complex ownership arrangement that saw team principal <a href="/wiki/Colin_Kolles" title="Colin Kolles">Colin Kolles</a> control the physical team, with Carabante owning the rights to the team's entry.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus_(2010%E2%80%9311)" title="Team Lotus (2010–11)">Lotus Racing</a> team principal <a href="/wiki/Tony_Fernandes" title="Tony Fernandes">Tony Fernandes</a> purchased the rights to the <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus" title="Team Lotus">Team Lotus</a> name from <a href="/wiki/David_Hunt_(racing_driver)" title="David Hunt (racing driver)">David Hunt</a>, with the intention of renaming the team to reflect its historical counterpart for the 2011 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Team_Lotus_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Team_Lotus-67">[67]</a></sup> The use of the Team Lotus name led to a <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus_(2010%E2%80%9311)#Use_of_Lotus_name" title="Team Lotus (2010–11)">naming dispute</a> with <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Cars" title="Lotus Cars">Lotus Cars</a>. The team announced that they had terminated their three-year contract with engine supplier <a href="/wiki/Cosworth" title="Cosworth">Cosworth</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lotus_engines_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lotus_engines-68">[68]</a></sup> and used <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_Sport_F1" title="Renault Sport F1">Renault</a> engines from 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></li>
<li>On 8 December 2010, <a href="/wiki/Lotus_Cars" title="Lotus Cars">Lotus Cars</a> announced a partnership with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_F1" title="Renault F1">Renault F1</a> that saw the British sports car manufacturer become title sponsor of the team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GL_Renault_3_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-GL_Renault_3-70">[70]</a></sup> with a view to taking full control over the next few years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GL_Renault_3_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-GL_Renault_3-70">[70]</a></sup> Confusion over the exact status over ownership of the team led team principal <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ric_Boullier" title="Éric Boullier">Éric Boullier</a> to clarify that <a href="/wiki/Genii_Capital" title="Genii Capital">Genii Capital</a> has full ownership of the team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> with former owners Renault retreating to a position as engine supplier. The team will be known as Lotus Renault GP,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GL_Renault_2_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-GL_Renault_2-72">[72]</a></sup> and the chassis and constructor will still be known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_F1" title="Renault F1">Renault</a> for reasons related to the <a href="/wiki/Concorde_Agreement" title="Concorde Agreement">Concorde Agreement</a>, similar to <a href="/wiki/Sauber" title="Sauber">Sauber</a> retaining the "BMW Sauber" name in <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_season" title="2010 Formula One season">2010</a> despite the departure of <a href="/wiki/Sauber#The_BMW_era_.28BMW_Sauber.2C_2006.E2.80.932009.29" title="Sauber">BMW</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/2009_Formula_One_season" title="2009 Formula One season">2009</a>.</li>
<li>In March 2011, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Infiniti" title="Infiniti">Infiniti</a>, the luxury brand of Japanese car manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Nissan" title="Nissan">Nissan</a> of whom <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> own a 44% stake, would become a major sponsor of <a href="/wiki/Red_Bull_Racing" title="Red Bull Racing">Red Bull Racing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> However, contradictory to early reports, the arrangement with Infiniti had not extended to an engine re-branding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_Sauber" title="BMW Sauber">BMW Sauber</a> announced in July 2010 that it will revert to the name Sauber in 2011. The team was forced to retain the BMW naming for 2010 due to issues involving television rights money that would not have been paid had the team changed their name.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sauber_name_change_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sauber_name_change-27">[27]</a></sup></li>
<li>After a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Williams_F1" title="Williams F1">Williams</a> demonstration run in <a href="/wiki/Caracas" title="Caracas">Caracas</a>, it was confirmed that Venezuelan state-controlled oil company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Petr%C3%B3leos_de_Venezuela" title="Petróleos de Venezuela">PDVSA</a> would enter into a long-term sponsorship deal with the team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> replacing outgoing sponsors <a href="/wiki/Royal_Bank_of_Scotland" title="Royal Bank of Scotland">RBS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philips" title="Philips">Philips</a> and <a href="/wiki/AirAsia" title="AirAsia">AirAsia</a>. <a href="/wiki/AirAsia" title="AirAsia">AirAsia</a> officially left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Williams_F1" title="Williams F1">Williams F1</a> to concentrate on <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus_(2010%E2%80%9311)" title="Team Lotus (2010–11)">Team Lotus</a>.</li>
<li>After sponsoring the team for the <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_season" title="2010 Formula One season">2010 season</a>, Russian sports car manufacturer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marussia" title="Marussia">Marussia</a> acquired what they termed a "significant stake" of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Racing" title="Virgin Racing">Virgin Racing</a>, with the team changing its name to Marussia Virgin Racing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marussia_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Marussia-45">[45]</a></sup> Further reports confirmed that Marussia had purchased a controlling stake in the team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> securing their future until 2014. The team split with <a href="/wiki/Wirth_Research" title="Wirth Research">Wirth Research</a> mid-season after a technical review by former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_F1" title="Renault F1">Renault F1 Team</a> engineering director <a href="/wiki/Pat_Symonds" title="Pat Symonds">Pat Symonds</a> found that Virgin's <a href="/wiki/Computational_fluid_dynamics" title="Computational fluid dynamics">CFD-only</a> approach had failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In the week before the <a href="/wiki/2011_British_Grand_Prix" title="2011 British Grand Prix">British Grand Prix</a>, Virgin announced a technical partnership with <a href="/wiki/McLaren" title="McLaren">McLaren</a> that granted them access to McLaren's testing facilities as well as the purchase of Wirth Research facilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Driver_changes">Driver changes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Formula_One_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Driver changes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>DAMS <a href="/wiki/GP2_Series" title="GP2 Series">GP2</a> driver <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_d%27Ambrosio" title="Jérôme d'Ambrosio">Jérôme d'Ambrosio</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Lucas_di_Grassi" title="Lucas di Grassi">Lucas di Grassi</a> at <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Racing" title="Virgin Racing">Virgin Racing</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jerome_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jerome-49">[49]</a></sup> having previously driven for the team during Friday practice sessions at selected events in <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_season" title="2010 Formula One season">2010</a>. Di Grassi did not have his contract with <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Racing" title="Virgin Racing">Virgin Racing</a> renewed. With only a handful of vacant racing seats available ahead of the winter testing period, he announced that would concentrate on a return to the sport in <a href="/wiki/2012_Formula_One_season" title="2012 Formula One season">2012</a> rather than attempt to secure a seat in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Deutsche_Tourenwagen_Masters_season" title="2010 Deutsche Tourenwagen Masters season">DTM</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Paul_di_Resta" title="Paul di Resta">Paul di Resta</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Vitantonio_Liuzzi" title="Vitantonio Liuzzi">Vitantonio Liuzzi</a> at <a href="/wiki/Force_India" title="Force India">Force India</a>, having previously driven for the team during Friday practice sessions at selected events in <a href="/wiki/2010_Formula_One_season" title="2010 Formula One season">2010</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Force11_26-3"><a href="#cite_note-Force11-26">[26]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nico_H%C3%BClkenberg" title="Nico Hülkenberg">Nico Hülkenberg</a> was dropped by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Williams_F1" title="Williams F1">Williams</a> on the eve of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Abu_Dhabi_Grand_Prix" title="2010 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix">2010 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> After turning down offers from several teams, including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">HRT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Racing" title="Virgin Racing">Virgin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hulk_Virgin_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hulk_Virgin-81">[81]</a></sup> Hülkenberg joined Force India as test and reserve driver.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Force11_26-4"><a href="#cite_note-Force11-26">[26]</a></sup> As a part of his arrangement with the team, Hülkenberg will drive a <a href="/wiki/Force_India_VJM04" title="Force India VJM04">VJM04</a> in the Friday morning free practice session of each Grand Prix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Narain_Karthikeyan" title="Narain Karthikeyan">Narain Karthikeyan</a> returned to Formula One with Hispania after last racing with <a href="/wiki/Jordan_Grand_Prix" title="Jordan Grand Prix">Jordan Grand Prix</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Formula_One_season" title="2005 Formula One season">2005</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Narain_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-Narain-40">[40]</a></sup> which was run at the time by Hispania team principal Colin Kolles. Karthikeyan also collaborated with Kolles on an unsuccessful attempt at the <a href="/wiki/2009_24_Hours_of_Le_Mans" title="2009 24 Hours of Le Mans">2009 24 Hours of Le Mans</a>, and he competed in the <a href="/wiki/2010_NASCAR_Camping_World_Truck_Series" title="2010 NASCAR Camping World Truck Series">2010 NASCAR Camping World Truck Series</a> in a limited campaign. He also competed in an <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_A1_Grand_Prix_season" title="2007–08 A1 Grand Prix season">A1GP</a> season for India.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Kubica" title="Robert Kubica">Robert Kubica</a> was injured while competing in the Ronde di Andora rally during the winter off-season, leaving him with multiple fractures to his arm, hand and leg. The nature of his injuries were serious enough to prevent him from starting the season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> while the surgeon who operated on Kubica has said that his recovery could take up to an entire year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> His former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BMW_Sauber" title="BMW Sauber">BMW Sauber</a> team-mate <a href="/wiki/Nick_Heidfeld" title="Nick Heidfeld">Nick Heidfeld</a> was later confirmed as his replacement at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lotus_Renault_GP" title="Lotus Renault GP">Lotus Renault GP</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NickLRGP_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-NickLRGP-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
<li>After being released from his contract with <a href="/wiki/Force_India" title="Force India">Force India</a> one year in advance of its expiration, <a href="/wiki/Vitantonio_Liuzzi" title="Vitantonio Liuzzi">Vitantonio Liuzzi</a> officially joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania Racing</a> as their second driver at the final test of the season, filling the last vacant racing seat on the grid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liuzzi_HRT_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Liuzzi_HRT-43">[43]</a></sup> As a result of this, Hispania's part-time racing drivers <a href="/wiki/Karun_Chandhok" title="Karun Chandhok">Karun Chandhok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christian_Klien" title="Christian Klien">Christian Klien</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sakon_Yamamoto" title="Sakon Yamamoto">Sakon Yamamoto</a> were all unable to secure contracts to race.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_GP2_Series_season" title="2010 GP2 Series season">2010 GP2 Series</a> champion <a href="/wiki/Pastor_Maldonado" title="Pastor Maldonado">Pastor Maldonado</a> was signed by Williams after testing for the team in the young driver tests in Abu Dhabi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williams_announces_Maldonado_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Williams_announces_Maldonado-25">[25]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sergio_P%C3%A9rez" title="Sergio Pérez">Sergio Pérez</a>, runner-up in the GP2 Series for <a href="/wiki/Addax_Team" title="Addax Team">Barwa Addax</a>, was signed by <a href="/wiki/Sauber" title="Sauber">Sauber</a> to partner <a href="/wiki/Kamui_Kobayashi" title="Kamui Kobayashi">Kamui Kobayashi</a>. His signing coincided with the announcement of a partnership between <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>'s telecommunications group <a href="/wiki/Telmex" title="Telmex">Telmex</a> and the Sauber team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sauber_partnership_with_Telmex_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sauber_partnership_with_Telmex-85">[85]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bruno_Senna" title="Bruno Senna">Bruno Senna</a> left <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania Racing</a> after a single season. Comments made by team principal <a href="/wiki/Colin_Kolles" title="Colin Kolles">Colin Kolles</a> suggested that the nephew of three-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Formula_One_World_Champions" title="List of Formula One World Champions">World Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Ayrton_Senna" title="Ayrton Senna">Ayrton Senna</a> had a strained relationship with the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Senna was later confirmed to have joined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_F1" title="Renault F1">Lotus Renault GP</a> as a part of their test and reserve team,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senna_Renault_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Senna_Renault-20">[20]</a></sup> and is the first in line to take over driving duties should either of the team's established drivers be unable to race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sakon_Yamamoto" title="Sakon Yamamoto">Sakon Yamamoto</a> moved from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania Racing</a> as a full-time driver to become a test driver for <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Racing" title="Virgin Racing">Virgin Racing</a> for the first three races after he was unable to secure a contract to continue racing with Hispania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yamamoto_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yamamoto-88">[88]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Mid-season changes</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pedro_de_la_Rosa" title="Pedro de la Rosa">Pedro de la Rosa</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Sergio_P%C3%A9rez" title="Sergio Pérez">Sergio Pérez</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Canadian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Canadian Grand Prix">Canadian Grand Prix</a> due to Pérez feeling unwell after the first practice session, following a heavy crash at the previous round in Monaco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dlrcan_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-dlrcan-30">[30]</a></sup></li>
<li>On 30 June, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania Racing</a> announced that Australian <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ricciardo" title="Daniel Ricciardo">Daniel Ricciardo</a> – at the time testing and reserve driver for <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Toro_Rosso" title="Scuderia Toro Rosso">Scuderia Toro Rosso</a> and racing for <a href="/wiki/ISR_Racing" title="ISR Racing">ISR</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_Formula_Renault_3.5_Series_season" title="2011 Formula Renault 3.5 Series season">Formula Renault 3.5 Series</a> – would be replacing <a href="/wiki/Narain_Karthikeyan" title="Narain Karthikeyan">Narain Karthikeyan</a> for the remainder of the 2011 season<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ricciardo_HRT_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ricciardo_HRT-41">[41]</a></sup> in what was described as an audition for a future race seat with <a href="/wiki/Scuderia_Toro_Rosso" title="Scuderia Toro Rosso">Scuderia Toro Rosso</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karun_Chandhok" title="Karun Chandhok">Karun Chandhok</a> returned to Formula One, replacing <a href="/wiki/Jarno_Trulli" title="Jarno Trulli">Jarno Trulli</a> at <a href="/wiki/Team_Lotus_(2010%E2%80%9311)" title="Team Lotus (2010–11)">Team Lotus</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_German_Grand_Prix" title="2011 German Grand Prix">German Grand Prix</a>, having previously fulfilled a Friday testing role in <a href="/wiki/2011_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Australian Grand Prix">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_Turkish_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Turkish Grand Prix">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011_European_Grand_Prix" title="2011 European Grand Prix">Valencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/2011_British_Grand_Prix" title="2011 British Grand Prix">Silverstone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Karun_racing_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Karun_racing-39">[39]</a></sup> Chandhok's last race meeting had been the <a href="/wiki/2010_British_Grand_Prix" title="2010 British Grand Prix">2010 British Grand Prix</a> when he raced for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispania_Racing" title="Hispania Racing">Hispania</a>. Trulli returned to the car for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Hungarian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Hungarian Grand Prix">Hungarian Grand Prix</a>.</li>
<li>On 24 August, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Senna" title="Bruno Senna">Bruno Senna</a> would replace <a href="/wiki/Nick_Heidfeld" title="Nick Heidfeld">Nick Heidfeld</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renault_F1" title="Renault F1">Renault</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Belgian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Belgian Grand Prix">Belgian</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Senna_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Senna-22">[22]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2011_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Italian Grand Prix">Italian</a> Grands Prix,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> leading to uncertainty over the status of the seat from the <a href="/wiki/2011_Singapore_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Singapore Grand Prix">Singapore Grand Prix</a> onwards. The team cited Heidfeld's failure to deliver speed to take on the role of a strong leader as the reason for his dismissal, rather than financial reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Renault indicated that they wished for Senna to race for the rest of the season, but "legal issues" threatened Senna's contract with the team. On 2 September, Renault confirmed that Heidfeld's contract had been legally terminated and Senna would drive alongside Vitaly Petrov for the remainder of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></li>
<li>Narain Karthikeyan returned to Hispania for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Indian_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Indian Grand Prix">Indian Grand Prix</a>, replacing <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Ricciardo" title="Daniel Ricciardo">Daniel Ricciardo</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> in the 22 car which meant Ricciardo replaced Liuzzi in the 23 car. Liuzzi returned to the team for the <a href="/wiki/2011_Abu_Dhabi_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Abu Dhabi Grand Prix">Abu Dhabi Grand Prix</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_calendar">Season calendar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2011_Formula_One_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Season calendar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 16 April 2010, <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Ecclestone" title="Bernie Ecclestone">Bernie Ecclestone</a> confirmed that there would be twenty races in 2011; all the races from the 2010 season and the addition of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Grand_Prix" title="Indian Grand Prix">Indian Grand Prix</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India_2011_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-India_2011-2">[2]</a></sup> A provisional calendar was announced on 8 September 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMSC080910_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMSC080910-93">[93]</a></sup> which was confirmed on 3 November 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WMSC031110_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-WMSC031110-94">[94]</a></sup> This was later revised to nineteen races with the postponement and later cancellation of the <a href="/wiki/2011_Bahrain_Grand_Prix" title="2011 Bahrain Grand Prix">Bahrain Grand Prix</a>.</p>
